Dear Mr Hiyakumoto
Geolabs Hawaii is pleased to submit our Geotechnical Engineering Report for the
Palau Compact Road Package D project on the Island of Babeldaob in the Republic of
geotechnical engineering exploration effort performed for the East West and North
Routes of the Palau Compact Road and presents our geotechnical engineering
recommendations for the Package D project
This geotechnical engineering report is intended to provide geotechnical
engineering design parameters for design of earthwork bridge foundations drainage
structures and pavements in support of the Package D project Due to the long linear
feature of this roadway project the roadway traverses varying subsurface conditions
The subsurface materials encountered at the project site consist primarily of high
moisture tropical soils which will present a unique set of difficulties to earthwork
operations in this wet environment Therefore special attention should be given to the
recommendations presented for the various conditions anticipated for the project
Detailed discussion and our geotechnical engineering design recommendations are
presented in the body of this report
The recommendations presented in this report are based on limited subsurface
exploration and laboratory testing programs Consequently variations between the
anticipated and actual subsurface conditions will likely be encountered in some areas
during construction Therefore it is imperative that experienced geotechnical engineers
and a qualified technical staff be present at the site during construction to observe and
implement the intent of the geotechnical recommendations presented herein We would
appreciate the opportunity of being engaged to observe the critical geotechnical related
items such as review of submittals observation of test pile and production pile driving
observation of soft soil treatment and observation of the fill test section

SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Based on our literature research site reconnaissance and field exploration
performed for Package D of the proposed Palau Compact Road project we anticipate
that the proposed roadway alignments will traverse various volcanic sedimentary and
alluvial lagoonal deposits ranging from very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formation to medium stiff to very stiff saprolite and old alluvial soils and to very soft
and or loose recent alluvial mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal deposits
Based on our field exploration the primary geotechnical engineering
considerations for design of the proposed roadway project include slope failure or
block type landslides of the cut slopes potential for rock excavation high moisture
contents of the in situ soils seepage of groundwater settlement of the fill materials due to
self weight settlement due to soft soil conditions erosion control pavement subgrade
stabilization and design of bridge foundations Special attention should be given to the
recommendations presented in this report to reduce the impacts of these geotechnical
engineering considerations on the proposed roadway project
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed roadway
alignments we believe that a cut slope inclination of one horizontal to one vertical
1H 1V may be used for the design of the planned cut slopes It should be noted that the
cut slopes for the North Route traversing the very dense volcanic breccia and tuff rock
formation may be designed with a cut slope ratio as steep as Where the
W O 3595 00 D Page 1
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
cut slope ratio is used for design of the rock slopes a rockfall catchment ditch
should be provided at the toe of the rock cut slope to reduce the adverse impacts of
rockfall on the roadway
In general fill slopes should be designed with a slope inclination of 2H 1V or
flatter Fill slopes with a vertical height of 4 meters or less may be steepened to a slope
inclination of if necessary except in areas where soft subsoils are anticipated
Where the fill slope exceeds 4 meters in vertical height soil reinforcements such as
geogrids or similar reinforcing materials should be incorporated into the design of these
fill slopes Fill slopes may also be steepened to as steep as 1H 1V provided
that adequate soil reinforcements are incorporated into the fill slope design
Geolabs Hawaii should be consulted to provide site specific recommendations for cut
slopes steeper than 1H 1V and fill slopes steeper than 2H 1V based on the actual subsoil
conditions encountered and the proposed slope design layout
Due to the high in situ moisture contents of the on site soils substantial aeration of
the high moisture soils will be required in order to achieve the normal 90 percent
compaction requirement and may not be feasible due to the year round high rainfall
experienced at the project site As a result the compaction requirements for general fill
placement will have to be reduced in order to aid in the earthwork construction using the
high moisture tropical soils in this wet environment Based on our engineering analyses
we believe that a compaction requirement of a minimum of 85 percent relative
compaction may be used for this project Based on this compaction requirement we
estimate that the on site saprolite materials may experience a decrease in volume on the
order of about 20 to 25 percent when excavated and placed as general fill In addition
when the high moisture soils are placed as fill at a lower compaction requirement the fills
will settle due to compression by self weight Therefore a settlement waiting period and
a settlement monitoring program is recommended for deep fills during construction prior
to pavement construction
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Our laboratory test results indicate that the in situ saprolite soils or compacted fills
composed of the same materials generally exhibit relatively low CBR values in a very
moist to wet condition Strengthening of these subgrade soils with the inclusion of
additives such as cement or lime treatment and or the incorporation of ground
stabilization fabrics at the subgrade level may be required prior to pavement construction
and or to facilitate earthwork construction with the very high moisture soils
Where the roadway alignment traverses soft and or unstable ground such as
swamps and mangroves we recommend that these areas be stabilized by placement of
a working platform prior to fill placement Depending on the soft soil thickness and the
planned fill heights substantial settlements of over 1 meter in magnitude may occur as a
result of the consolidation of the soft soil deposits under new fill loads Settlements on
the order of about 0 1 to 1 0 meter have been estimated for some soft soil areas identified
in Package D during our field exploration Embankments in soft soil areas should be
over filled to account for the anticipated amount of soft ground and fill settlements
A surcharge program with settlement monitoring may be considered to reduce the
settlement period and subsequent long term settlements in these conditions
Because some localized areas of the Package D roadway alignment are underlain
by significant amounts of soft soils with substantial fill thickness we recommend that
stage construction similar to a fill surcharge program be implemented for construction
of the fill embankment in these soft soil areas to reduce the potential for shear failure and
slope instability However the stage construction will have an impact on the overall
construction schedule and phasing of the project We recommend that where stage
construction is considered the filling and surcharging of the soft soil areas be designated
as a Phase 1 item of work which is to be initiated as soon as the project commences to
allow the soft soils to consolidate
We anticipate that permanent drainage structures located in these soft soil areas
will be subjected to a substantial amount of settlements which will reduce the hydraulic
capacity of the drainage structures In order to reduce the effects of the substantial
settlements on the drainage structures we recommend that the soft soils underneath the
W O 3595 00 D GEOLARS HAWAII Page 3
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
drainage structures be removed and replaced with suitable backfill materials prior to
construction of the drainage structures For drainage structures with thinner fills less
than about 5 meters the fill embankment may be constructed with a temporary drainage
structure followed by a settlement waiting period to allow the settlements to occur After
the settlements have occurred and are near equilibrium the temporary drainage structure
is excavated and removed followed by construction of the permanent drainage structure
This method of construction to accommodate the ground settlements is recommended for
the circulation box culverts at the causeway embankment
The on site soils are silty in nature and are highly susceptible to erosion
In addition to the construction of earth berms interceptor drainage ditches and slope
planting other erosion control measures such as conventional grouted rubble paving and
concrete lining may be considered for the subject project especially in localized areas
where concentration of surface water run off is evident In addition flexible geosynthetic
matting may offer a viable solution for slope erosion control problems by promoting
mulching reducing run off velocity and establishing temporary and permanent erosion
control on the slope face
For design and cost estimation purposes it is our opinion that a flexible pavement
section consisting of asphalt concrete pavement over aggregate base course on subbase
course may be used for the proposed roadway design Alternatively a pavement section
consisting of asphalt concrete pavement over cement treated base on subbase course
may also be considered for the subject roadway Pavement sections for different Traffic
Indices for the Package D alignments have been included in this report for use in
construction
To reduce the potential for premature pavement failure due to saturation of the
base subbase and subgrade soils longitudinal edge drains should be considered along
the roadway alignment with relatively flat gradients generally less than 2 percent and in
areas where poor drainage may be anticipated Installation of transverse drains at low
spots along the roadway alignments and ford crossings is also recommended
SECTION EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Based on the field exploration results and the foundation loads provided we
believe that the proposed causeway bridge may be supported by a composite foundation
system consisting of shallow foundations and driven pile foundations The south
abutment and center pier may be supported on shallow foundations bearing on the rock
formation whereas the north abutment will need to be supported on driven pile
foundations Construction of the causeway embankment at the north bridge abutment
may require the use of stage construction to reduce the potential for shear failure and or
slope instability We recommend that construction of the north abutment foundations be
delayed until the abutment fill has reached a state of equilibrium under the new fill loads
Detailed discussions of these items and our geotechnical engineering design
recommendations are presented in the following sections of this report
END OF EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

SECTION Il GENERAL
This report presents the results of our geotechnical engineering exploration
performed for the Package D portion of the proposed Palau Compact Road project on the
island of Babeldaob in the Republic of Palau The general location and the vicinity of the
island of Babeldaob and the Republic of Palau are shown on the Project Location and
Vicinity Map Plate 1
This report summarizes our findings and geotechnical engineering
recommendations resulting from our literature research site reconnaissance field
exploration laboratory testing and engineering analyses performed for Package D of the
proposed Palau Compact Road project These findings and geotechnical engineering
recommendations are intended for design and preliminary cost estimation purposes only
The findings and recommendations presented herein are subject to the limitations noted
at the end of this report
A Project Considerations
It is desired to improve the existing roadway system on the island of Babeldaob in
the Republic of Palau with the construction of approximately 85 kilometers of new
roadway and associated structures known as the Palau Compact Road project
The proposed Palau Compact Road project will involve the design and construction of a
two lane two way rural collector road in general accordance with U S standards with
optimum operation and maintenance characteristics including pavements roadside
drainage cross drainage bridges shoulders guardrails pavement markings signage
drainage markers kilometer markers and intersections Roadway lighting and signal
lights sidewalks and curbs are not required elements for the proposed project
Based on the scope of work provided the proposed Palau Compact Road project
will consist of four design packages designated as Packages A through D as shown on
the General Site Plan Plate 2 A preliminary geotechnical engineering exploration for the
SECTION II GENERAL
entire Palau Compact Road project was conducted by our office and the findings and
preliminary recommendations were presented in the report entitled Preliminary
Geotechnical Engineering Report Palau Compact Road Island of Babeldaob Republic
of Palau DACW83 97 C 0006 dated Subsequently we have
conducted a design level geotechnical engineering exploration to obtain additional
information for the formulation of geotechnical engineering recommendations pertinent to
the detailed design of each package This report presents the findings and geotechnical
engineering recommendations pertinent to Package D of the Palau Compact Road
project
Package D of the Palau Compact Road project will consist of approximately
20 kilometers of new roadway and associated structures including the following
segments
e The East West Route approximately 6 kilometers long beginning at the
intersection with the West Route in Ngardmau State proceeding east and
terminating at the intersection with the East Route in Ngaraard State
e The North Route approximately 14 kilometers long will include the
following segments
Beginning northward from the intersection with the East West
Route and proceeding to the southern end of the Ngaraard
Causeway for approximately 7 5 kilometers
Ngaraard Causeway approximately 0 5 kilometers long
Continuing from the northern end of the Ngaraard Causeway
northward and proceeding to an intersection with an existing road
approximately 6 kilometers long
Based on the alignment and rolling topography along this package maximum cuts
on the order of about 26 meters deep and fills of about 20 meters thick are anticipated for
Package D We anticipate that Package D will also include the design and construction
of numerous box and pipe culvert crossings The Ngaraard Causeway will require
placement of approximately 2 to 3 meters of fills about 6 meters for the bridge abutment
over water and soft soils and construction of a two span bridge structure

B Purpose and Scope

proposed Palau Compact Road project was to obtain a general overview of the surface

with our revised fee proposal dated The scope of our work included

SECTION Ill SITE CHARACTERIZATION
The islands of Palau are a part of Micronesia located in the western portion of
the North Pacific Ocean as shown on the Project Location and Vicinity Map Plate 1 It
lies approximately 885 kilometers to the east of Mindanao Philippines and about
1 300 kilometers to the southwest of Guam The Palau Islands consist of a small
elongated arc shaped island chain in the Western Caroline Islands which trend
generally north to south extending from Latitude 8 degrees 12 minutes North to
Latitude 6 degrees 53 minutes North and from Longitude 134 degrees 8 minutes East
to Longitude 134 degrees 44 minutes East The major islands comprising the Republic
of Palau generally trend in a north south direction and consist of Babeldaob Koror
Peleliu and Angaur The general location and vicinity of the
Republic of Palau are shown on the Project Location and Vicinity Map Plate 1
The proposed Palau Compact Road project is located on the island of
Babeldaob which lies approximately 2 kilometers north of Koror across the Toachel
Channel Koror is the capital and main city of the Republic of Palau The island of
Babeldaob is composed of ten states including
and Airai as shown
on the General Site Plan Plate 2 The island of Babeldaob was connected to the island
of Koror by a bridge locally known as the Koror Babeldaob K B Bridge which provided
the only access for vehicles between the islands
In September 1996 the K B Bridge catastrophically collapsed leaving the islands
separated and without means for vehicular traffic Shortly thereafter the primary
means of commuting between the islands was established by the government which
began operating barge and ferry service transportation In August 1997 a temporary
floating bridge was completed and opened for public use The floating bridge is
anticipated to remain in use until a new permanent bridge can be designed and
constructed
SECTION Ill SITE CHARACTERIZATION
A Geography
The Palau Islands form a curved chain of islands totaling about 350 in number
and covering approximately 458 square kilometers in area The island chain extends
approximately 161 kilometers in length and 64 kilometers in width Babeldaob the
largest island of the chain is an elongated volcanic island trending north to south and
encompasses about 208 square kilometers of land area Elevations on Babeldaob
range from sea level along the coastal areas to about 242 meters Mean Sea Level
MSL at Mt Ngerekelehuus on the northwestern side of Babeldaob
The Palau Reef encircles the island of Babeldaob as a barrier and fringing reef
creating extensive quiet water lagoons and bays with some deep channels and
passages adjacent to the island Beyond the fringing reef the ocean floor drops
steeply to greater than 300 meters in depth within a distance of about 1 kilometer
The island of Babeldaob is primarily of volcanic origin with some localized
occurrence of limestone rock formation particularly in southern coastal Babeldaob
The relief is generally characterized by hilly terrain of elongated ridgelines frequently
incised by streams and gullies exposing extremely weathered volcanic earth materials
Flatter alluvial areas are restricted mainly to the mouths and banks of larger streams
and along the coastline situated behind sandy beaches where inland hills do not
abruptly terminate at the shoreline More rugged terrain consisting of sharp ridges and
cliff lines occur on the western and southeastern portions of the island Both rounded
hilltops and sharp ridgelines rise above the generally rolling terrain at scattered
locations offering prominent geographic landmarks among the generally homogenous
backdrop
The coastline of Babeldaob is irregularly shaped with many small bays and
elevated headlands Swamp areas consisting of dense mangrove within shallow
tidal influenced mudflats exist throughout approximately 70 percent of the coastline
areas The width of the mangrove swamps along the coastline varies from less than
10 meters to greater than 800 meters in some places The mangrove swamps
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
encompass much of the lowland coastline and large areas bordering the bays and
estuaries Marsh areas exist in some inland areas generally bordering major river
systems and broad basins
The drainage pattern on Babeldaob is essentially trellised with the larger streams
and rivers aligned with the longitudinal axis of the island Ngermeskang River is the
longest river measuring about 15 8 kilometers in length which flows into Karamando
Bay from the northeast The Ngerdok River is the largest watershed on Babeldaob
encompassing some 29 square kilometers in area
B Climate
The Palau Islands have a maritime tropical rainy climate characterized by small
seasonal changes Temperatures are generally uniform throughout the year with
abundant rainfall reaching a maximum in July and a minimum from February through
April The mean annual temperature is about 27 degrees Celsius with a relative
humidity of about 82 percent
Rainfall typically occurs as intense showers of relatively short duration and
averages about 250 to 500 mm per month Periods of prolonged heavy rainfall lasting
several days at a time occur as typhoon storm centers frequently pass to the north of
Palau during the summer months Other pronounced rainy periods occur as the
equatorial convergent zone advances northward within the vicinity of Palau around
June and July and again in September and October as the convergent zone retreats
southward
C Regional Geologic Setting
The Philippine Sea and the Pacific Ocean Basin are separated by a series of
elongated submarine ridge structures The Palau Islands are situated at the exposed
crest of the southwestern most submarine ridge of the area The Palau ridge is part of
the Palau Kyushu ridge which extends from Kyushu Japan southward towards Palau
where a complementary trench structure forms to the southeast of Palau These ridge
and trench structures constitute the Palau Arc The eastern slope of the Palau Ridge
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
slopes steeply to the Palau trench which plunges to about 8 200 meters at about
48 kilometers east of the north end of the Palau Islands The west flank of the ridge
slopes gradually to a depth of about 5 500 meters at about 400 kilometers to the west
The andesite line which marks the margin of the western Pacific Basin has
been positioned along the eastern edge of the Palau trench This demarcation
separates the region of predominantly andesitic volcanism to the west from the Pacific
Basin region of basaltic volcanism The area is also a major structural and
physiographic boundary between the two regions
The structure of the Palau Islands reflects their situation as the exposed crest of
the Palau Ridge The islands elongated form has resulted from volcanic emissions and
deposition of pyroclastic materials along the arcuate ridge structure Due to the varied
locations of the volcanic sources and the amount of emissions the successive
accumulation of pyroclastic materials was highly irregular in occurrence In addition
most of the eruptions were subaqueous resulting in submarine landslides and slumps
and contributing to the deformed and highly irregular character of the depositional
surfaces
D Geology of Babeldaob
Babeldaob Island exists as a result of the accumulation of volcanic materials
along the crest of the Palau Ridge The form of the island is principally controlled by
many factors which include 1 faulting associated with past tectonic activity
2 numerous historic land submergence and emergence as a result of sea level
fluctuation 3 submarine erosion 4 erosion by streams and 5 deep tropical
weathering of volcanic materials comprising the island
In general Babeldaob consists of a central strip of the oldest volcanic rock
overlapped on the east by the next younger unit and separated by a fault zone on the
west from the youngest volcanic rocks which are arranged in a rough circle around a
former caldera at Karamando Bay The regional ridge and trench structure extensive
volcanism and the presence of numerous faults cutting the pyroclastic deposits confirm
W O 3595 00 D GEOLAGS HAWAII Page 14
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
past tectonic activity However at the present time there is little evidence of on going
deformation of the island arc system
Based on the Geology Map of Babelthuap and Adjacent Islands Palau Islands
prepared by the U S Army and the U S Geological Survey the geologic materials
mapped on Babeldaob include various volcanic alluvial and estuarine lagoonal or
beach deposits The most recent earth material deposits include man made fills
mangrove swamp mud alluvial sediments and coralline beach deposits These
materials continue to be deposited at the present time Terrestrial and marine
sediments deposited in historic Miocene through Pleistocene time include the alluvial
Airai clay with interbedded lignite and the Palau limestone formation The volcanic
materials comprise the oldest deposits and consist of the Babeldaob Aimeliik and
Ngeremlengui formations These volcanic units comprise the bulk of the land area on
Babeldaob Island
The Babeldaob formation consists of massive basaltic andesitic volcanic breccia
with some tuff breccia and layers of tuff U S Army 1956 Breccia is a coarse grained
volcanic rock composed of angular broken rock fragments or clasts welded together in
a finer grained mineral rock matrix Breccia is formed by volcanic explosions and or
debris flows of super heated rock mass Rocks and soils associated with this formation
exist as a large rectangular shaped area extending north northeast to south southwest
in central Babeldaob
The Aimeliik formation consists of andesitic basaltic volcanic breccias tuff
breccia and bedded tuffs and is divided into the Ngarsul and Ngardok members which
are composed of varying amounts of tuff and breccia materials U S Army 1956 The
formation underlies most of northeastern eastern and southern Babeldaob
The Ngeremlengui formation consists of andesitic and dacitic volcanic breccia
together with tuffs flows conglomerates and related sediments It is divided into three
members the Nghemesed dacitic volcanic breccia the
SECTION III SITE CHARACTERIZATION
volcanic breccia and the Arakabesan andesitic volcanic breccia U S Army 1956
The formation occurs as a broad strip of area along the west central and northwest side
of Babeldaob and along the northern tip of Arekalong Peninsula
Other volcanic rock types include intrusive geologic bodies such as dikes sills
and volcanic plugs which occur widely distributed in the volcanic units described
above The larger intrusive rock structures can be found in the area around
Karamando Bay associated with the most recent volcanic center of that area
U S Army 1956 Many of these intrusive features are less weathered than their
surrounding host rock material and are erosional remnants exhibited as prominent
outcroppings
Because of the humid tropical climate the volcanic rock exposed at the surface
is usually extremely weathered to substantial depths with fresh surface outcroppings of
rock being generally rare in occurrence The majority of the volcanic materials
observed on Babeldaob Island have been weathered to residual and saprolite soils with
only scattered localized pockets of hard indurated rock The deep tropical weathering
of the island has resulted in a mature stage topography with rounded rolling hills
separated by scoured stream channels
The volcanic rocks of Babeldaob have been extensively faulted during and
following their deposition Faulting is believed to have been a major factor in
determining the distribution of volcanic formations as many geologic contacts occur
along fault lines U S Army 1956 Post volcanic faulting has modified the distribution
of the geologic formations and is responsible for many physiographic features
Movement along the faults appeared to be similar to earlier tectonic movement
however the most recent movement is believed to be in response to new tectonic
forces which have since developed U S Army 1956 Based on the geologic map of
Babeldaob the larger fault zones curve to the northeast across the island forming
concave a cs

SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
In general the proposed Palau Compact Road Package D alignments including
the East West and North Routes were observed to traverse terrain underlain by four
main soil and rock materials of varying character and engineering properties The soil
and rock materials were identified during our geotechnical ground surface
reconnaissance of the alignments and during our subsurface exploration at selected
locations along the alignments
The geotechnical reconnaissance included visual observation of both naturally
occurring exposures of the ground surface and exposures created by the bulldozer
during the trail clearing operations related to the drilling exploration In addition manual
probing of the surficial soils were performed at selected locations along the alignments
to evaluate the consistency of the near surface soils As a result of our site
reconnaissance and subsurface exploration the soil and rock materials observed were
condensed and grouped into four major soil or rock types The four main soil or rock
types are listed below in the general order of the frequency of occurrence throughout
the project site The listing begins with the most common materials encountered at the
site and ends with the least common type of material encountered
e Saprolite Soil extremely weathered rock materials
e Volcanic Breccia or Tuff Rock Formation relatively unweathered rock
materials
e Lagoonal Deposit marine coralline materials
e Swamp Recent Alluvial Deposits organic mud and sediment
The following sections briefly describe the character of each of the above
generalized soil and rock types and how they relate to the soil and rock types outlined
in our Preliminary Geotechnical Engineering Report PGER dated
The relation is provided to serve as a link between the soil and rock descriptions
provided in our preliminary report and the condensed groups and descriptions of soil
and rock described in this report
W O 3595 00 D Page 17
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
A Saprolite Soil Extremely Weathered Rock
Saprolite is typical of the tropical weathering of volcanic rocks and is composed
mainly of silty materials The saprolite soil unit is the most dominant soil type traversed
by the East West and North Routes of the Palau Compact Road This soil unit consists
predominantly of reddish brown mottled with tan purple and gray clayey silt and silty
clay soils The saprolite soils may contain variations in color tan grayish white or
pinkish tan with varying degrees of mottling or colored striations depending on the type
of parent volcanic rock from which the soils are derived and the degree of chemical
weathering that the material has experienced The soils are essentially derived from
basaltic and andesitic breccia and tuff formations which may contain intrusive rock
bodies of variable composition
Bauxite gravel deposits consisting of a loose surface cover of brown and red
bauxite concretions are often found mantling the residual and saprolite soils Based on
our observations the bauxite gravel are generally confined to the drier upper slopes
and ridgelines of sparse vegetation The deposits are generally absent on lower hill
slopes and areas covered by dense forest vegetation The absence of bauxite gravel in
these areas may be attributed to higher soil moisture content and accelerated chemical
weathering processes The bauxite gravel is generally high in iron and aluminum
content The thickness of the bauxite deposits vary but are generally less than about
300 mm however local deposits were observed to be greater than 1 8 meters in
thickness
The occurrence of buried relatively unweathered hard rock such as massive
boulders or zones of less weathered rocky material localized intrusive volcanic bodies
such as dikes and sills and irregular transitions to underlying rock formation may occur
embedded within the saprolite soil type The occurrence of these rock zones within the
saprolite are common but they may be difficult to locate by surface observation and
may not be encountered by test borings
W O 3595 00 D Page 18
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
The saprolite soil unit described herein may be equated to Soil Types C D E
and F described in our PGER dated The Soil Types outlined in our
preliminary report have been revised and grouped together to simplify the classification
of the saprolite and residual soil geologic materials The reduction in the number of soil
types is due to similarities in the physical characteristics and engineering properties of
the various residual and saprolite soils encountered at the site
B Volcanic Breccia or Tuff Rock Formation Relatively Unweathered Rock
The volcanic breccia and tuff rock units occur as greenish to brownish gray
slightly fractured to massive hard rock formation The rock formations typically exist as
massive rounded outcroppings showing embedded breccia clasts or as layered
fractured often platy volcanic tuff
Volcanic breccia are angular pyroclastic rock materials erupted from vents as
either flows of superheated material or as blocks of superheated material larger than
60 mm in size that may be cemented with or without a volcanic material matrix
Volcanic tuff is formed by the deposition and cementation of relatively fine grained
pyroclastic materials such as sand and ash which accumulate as airfall deposits
during volcanic eruptions of superheated materials and gases Tuff formations often
show horizontal or inclined bedding which mimic the underlying topography that the
deposit accumulated These rock formations may be exposed at the ground surface
partially exposed and coexisting with some saprolite soil or buried under a relatively
thin mantle of surficial alluvium or residual soil
The rock formation unit described herein may be equated to Soil Rock Types A
and B described in our PGER The rock types outlined in our preliminary report have
been revised and condensed to simplify the classification of the rock formation
materials The reduction of rock types is due to similarities in the physical
characteristics and engineering properties of the various rock materials encountered at
the site
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
C Lagoonal Deposit
The lagoonal deposits at the site generally consist of gray white or tan silty
coralline sands and gravel with shells derived from coral reef and beach environments
Included within these deposits may be lenses of gray or brown clayey silts with gravel
or dark gray peat The lagoonal deposits are typically under consolidated and
accumulate as loose or soft deposits in submarine low energy environments such as
tidal influenced bays estuaries and lagoons The deposits accumulate as a result of
the transportation and deposition of broken coral reef materials and periodic influx of
terrestrial sediment and organic matter introduced from streams flowing into the shallow
water depositional environment The lagoonal deposit soil unit described herein may
be equated to Soil Type J described in our PGER
D Swamp and Recent Alluvial Deposits
Based on their characteristics and modes of deposition the swamp soils and
recent alluvial soils are closely related to each other in physical properties Both of
these soils generally exist as under consolidated soft to medium stiff deposits as a
result of their sedimentary deposition The swamp soils generally consist of dark brown
or dark gray organic rich silts and clayey silts with some sand and gravel These soils
may contain significant amounts of root and decomposed organic material peat as a
result of organic debris being buried during deposition The marsh and swamp deposits
are commonly found along the low lying coastal mangrove areas where streams meet
the shoreline environment and where shallow groundwater levels are largely influenced
by tidal fluctuation and stream discharge The ground surface within the swamp land
may be very soft existing as a slurry of mud and water or may be relatively firm as a
result of the intertwined matrix of root growth associated with mangrove vegetation
The recent alluvial deposits generally consist of tan to brown clayey silts and silty
clays derived from the erosion transportation and re deposition of saprolite and
residual soil materials Alluvial soils are generally found within some stream channels
and bordering some stream banks at the mouths outlets of streams and within broad
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
valley floors and basin features surrounded by hills These soils may also be found in
close proximity to swamp and lagoonal environments Furthermore recent alluvium
may be found interbedded with the swamp and lagoonal soil deposits
The swamp and recent alluvial soil unit described herein may be equated to Soil
Types H and described in our PGER Soil Types H and outlined in our preliminary
report have been condensed and regrouped to simplify the classification of the
materials encountered
E Existing Site Conditions
The following subsections contain descriptions of the existing surface conditions
and occurrence of soil and rock types observed along the Package D East West Route
and North Route alignments The progression of the site description has been
organized by geographic location and is referenced by the project station numbering of
the alignments
The existing site conditions were observed during a ground surface
reconnaissance of the alignment centerlines and existing dirt roads intersecting the
alignments The reconnaissance was performed under variable conditions of both wet
and dry weather which may have affected interpretation of some observations related
to the flowing condition of streams and location of soft ground conditions
1 East West Route to
The East West Route begins in Ngardmau State at the junction with the Package
C West Route and trends toward the east into Ngaraard State terminating at the
junction with the Package C East Route The East West Route traverses mainly
undeveloped forest and savanna land consisting of hilly inland terrain vegetated
by a dense forest canopy with localized patches of cleared land vegetated with
limited fern and shrub growth The alignment rises in elevation from Ngardmau
to traverse the upper slopes of a series of hills elongated east to west in
W O 3595 00 D Page 21
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
direction Beginning near and continuing eastward the alignment
declines in elevation down the side slopes of a large river valley to meet the
eastern coastline
Based on our field reconnaissance and boring information the East West Route
traverses ground underlain by saprolite soils derived from deep weathering of
both breccia rock formation and localized areas of tuff rock formation Significant
ground surface outcroppings of rock formation were not observed along this
route except within the bottoms of some deeply incised stream gullies It appears
as though scouring by stream erosion had exposed the breccia rock formation at
the channel invert At other locations rock formation was not observed at the
ground surface although much of the alignment was densely vegetated and
covered with significant accumulations of forest debris making continuous
observation difficult Borings drilled at locations throughout this route confirm
that rock formation may not be encountered at the ground surface but may be
encountered at variable depths in the subsurface below the saprolite horizon
The terrain underlain by the saprolite consists of an irregular topography of
ridgelines and eroded gullies Many of the deeper gullies exhibit perennial
stream flow whereas other smaller gullies appear to exhibit only intermittent
stream flow Alluvial deposits were observed to be generally thin and restricted
to flatter areas at the base of steep slopes The streams appeared to contain
little if any alluvial material due to the relatively steep stream gradients the
channelized flow character and the flash flood type of runoff experienced
In general the topographic lows including valleys gullies and basins show
much wetter surface soil conditions than the adjacent hills or ridgelines indicating
potential slow seepage or wicking of subsurface moisture and poor drying due to
the forest canopy In contrast the ground surface of the upper slopes and
ridgelines appeared to dry out between rainstorms

2 North Route to
The North Route begins in Ngaraard State at the junction with the Package D
East West Route trends northerly through Ngaraard and terminates in the
southern portion of Ngarchelong State This terminus marks the northern limit of
the Palau Compact Road project
The geomorphic form of northern Babeldaob is a narrow peninsula landform
extending from north to south with relatively shallow water lagoons on both the
eastern and western margins The North Route traverses variable elevations of
the inland terrain of the peninsula with the exception of a shallow lagoon
crossing at the site of the proposed Ngaraard Causeway through
The southern half of the North Route traverses undeveloped hilly terrain
separated by streams and vegetated by a dense forest canopy Scattered along
the alignment are areas where previous forest clearing and repeated burning
have occurred thus altering the landscape to expose the ground surface which
supports limited growth of fern shrubs and scattered pandanus trees savanna
The forests with localized savanna conditions generally exist from
through
The majority of the alignment traverses undeveloped land however the northern
half of the North Route about through traverses
partially developed land which includes the existing Babeldaob dirt road and
several villages with multiple dwellings and agricultural fields In addition the
topography along this portion of the alignment is gentler with more gradual
elevation changes containing vegetation types ranging from savanna to forest
growth
Based on our reconnaissance the North Route traverses ground surface which
may be underlain by saprolite soils rock formation lagoonal deposits and marsh

forest canopy and growth of a variety of trees shrubs and ground cover the soil
profile in forested areas may include the following

In comparison to forest environments the savanna environment is typically

and organic topsoil horizons
6 Typical Stream Channel Characteristics
Many of the stream channels observed crossing the alignments exhibit similar
characteristics In general two types of drainage morphologies were observed
The first type is typical of active perennial stream flow of moderate to high
discharge volume These streams are more commonly acting as primary mid to
lower reach well developed channels discharging larger size watersheds The
second drainage morphology appears as a result of generally lighter stream flow
W O 3595 00 D Page 28
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
or spring seepage and is contained within a broad U shaped gully The gully
contains a broader area of slower moving stream flow and seepage
Most of the perennial streams are situated within U shaped gullies incising
saprolite soil The active stream channel was often observed further incised at
the gully invert as a steep sided meandering trench exposing the geologic
character of the gully bottom The larger stream channel inverts were often
observed scoured to expose highly weathered and or slightly weathered hard
rock formation condition Alluvial deposits associated with perennial stream
channel morphology appear relatively insignificant
Most of the intermittent slower flowing streams exist within broad U shaped gully
bottoms covered by a dense matrix of intertwined roots and some surficial soft
alluvial deposits Commonly this drainage morphology was observed in the
upper weakly developed reaches of streams and locations where several gullies
converge to form a single broad drainage gully Alluvial soil accumulations and
the occurrence of a matrix of exposed root growth are more prevalent associated
with this stream morphology
F Subsurface Conditions
The subsurface conditions along the Package D alignments were explored by
drilling and sampling a total of 51 borings at the approximate locations shown on the
Site Plans Plates 3 1 through 3 3 In general the southern portion of the Package D
alignments traverses saprolite soils derived from intense weathering of the volcanic
breccia and tuff rock formation Based on the borings drilled in this area pockets of
variably weathered rock may be embedded within the saprolite soil These pockets
may contain saprolite material of a sandy or gravelly nature in contrast to the typical
clayey silt and silty clay saprolite soil composition In addition relatively unweathered
parent rock material or other volcanic intrusive rock may be locally embedded in the
saprolite soil matrix These rock bodies may exist as erosional remnant material The
W O 3595 00 D Page 29
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
erosional remnants may occur as boulders ranging in size from 1 meter to in excess of
about 6 meters
Based on the boring information hard rock formation consisting of volcanic
breccia and some tuff formation should be expected to be buried at variable depths
below the saprolite soils The depth to rock can be highly variable depending on the
local weathering and erosion rates In general rock formation underlying prominent
hills were encountered at depths ranging from about 12 to 20 meters below the ground
surface south of the proposed Ngaraard Causeway Rock formation was also
encountered at shallower depths on the order of about 2 to 4 meters below the ground
surface but these locations were generally restricted to topographic low locations
bordering streams or deeply incised gullies
Based on our exploration the majority of the alignment north of the proposed
Ngaraard Causeway may encounter significant hard rock formation at the ground
surface or buried at relatively shallow depths beneath the ground surface less than
2 meters below the ground surface This is in contrast to the alignment south of the
Ngaraard causeway where the rock formation is generally covered by a thicker
weathered profile However discrete zones along this portion of the alignment were
observed to exhibit mainly saprolite conditions at the ground surface
Our boring exploration of the causeway alignment generally revealed lagoonal
silty sand and gravel materials with interbedded clay seams Rock formation was
encountered at the boring locations nearest to the northern and southern shorelines
The rock formation was encountered underlying the lagoonal deposit and can be
correlated with rock outcroppings at the ground surface on the shoreline
Groundwater levels were encountered in some of the drilled borings at variable
depths below the existing ground surface at the time of our field exploration Generally
groundwater was encountered in borings drilled near active streams and in low elevations
near the coastline Groundwater levels can fluctuate depending on factors such as tidal
SECTION IV GEOTECHNICAL SURVEY
fluctuations seasonal rainfall presence of springs and or seepage storm surge
conditions time of year and other factors
Because of the high tropical rainfall coupled with low permeability soils surface
runoff is generally high However because of the infiltration that does occur seepage of
the downward percolating groundwater may be observed along the lower slopes of hills
and ridgelines The seepage areas are reflected by changes in the growth of vegetation
and the occurrence of perpetually moist ground surface conditions The seepage is
widespread and occasionally may produce a flowing spring where a layer of more
permeable soil or rock transmits the flow of water to the ground surface Other seepage
may occur at the interface where saprolite soil is in abrupt contact with underlying
massive rock formation
Detailed descriptions of the field exploration methodology is presented in
Appendix A of this report Descriptions and graphic representation of the materials
encountered in the drilled borings are provided on the Logs of Borings Plates A 1 1
through A 51 1 Laboratory tests were performed on selected samples and the results
are presented in Appendix B

SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
Based on our literature research site reconnaissance and field exploration
performed for Package D of the Palau Compact Road project we anticipate that the
proposed roadway alignments will traverse various volcanic sedimentary and
alluvial lagoonal deposits The observed soil rock materials ranged from very dense
volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock formation to medium stiff to very stiff saprolite soils
and to very soft and or loose recent alluvial mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal
deposits
The earthwork for this project constitutes a major portion of the construction costs
Therefore the design slopes for cuts and fills have a significant impact on the construction
budget Flatter conservative slope ratios generally increase slope stability However in
the mountainous terrain along the proposed roadway alignment flatter slope ratios result
in greatly increased earthwork quantities and erosion potential Therefore for this project
somewhat steeper slope ratios have been adopted We believe that the reduced
earthwork quantities and reduced erosion potential outweigh the potential for localized
sloughing of some of the steeper cut and fill slopes However a more vigorous slope
repair and roadway maintenance effort should be expected for the roadway
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed alignments we
believe that slope inclinations of 1H 1V and 2H 1V may be used for the design of the
planned cut and fill slopes respectively We believe that a cut slope inclination steeper
than 1H 1V may be feasible in areas where very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formations are encountered Depending on the heights of the planned fill slopes fill slopes
may be designed with a slope inclination as steep as 1H 1V except in soft soil areas
provided that adequate soil reinforcements are incorporated into the fill material
Geolabs Hawaii should be consulted to provide site specific recommendations pertaining
to cut and fill slopes with a slope inclination steeper than the general values recommended
above
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
We wish to emphasize that drainage features such as interceptor drainage ditches
subdrains road gutters and longitudinal edge drains are critical to the stability of the cut
and fill slopes and performance of the pavement structure Excessive surface run off over
the slope face may cause erosion of the exposed soils thus potentially jeopardizing the
long term stability and performance of the cut and fill slopes Accumulation of water below
the pavement structural section will soften the silty and clayey subgrade soils and cause
premature failure of the pavement structure Therefore it is our opinion that special
attention should be given to the design and implementation of these drainage features
along the proposed roadway alignments
Construction of a causeway embankment between and of
the North Route is anticipated for Package D The causeway embankment will be
constructed over soft loose lagoonal deposits Therefore placement of the causeway fills
should be initiated as early as possible to allow the existing ground to adjust to the new fill
loads A settlement waiting period will need to be specified in the contract documents and
a settlement monitoring program should be implemented to evaluate the magnitude and
rate of the estimated settlements prior to construction of the pavement section and
improvements such as the causeway bridge foundations abutments and culverts on the
causeway fills A surcharge program may be considered to accelerate the consolidation of
the underlying soft loose soils to reduce the settlement waiting period
For the purpose of our discussions fill height is defined as the vertical distance
between the top and toe elevations of the fill slope whereas fill thickness is defined as the
vertical distance between the existing ground and the finished grade at any point Detailed
discussion of these items and our geotechnical engineering design recommendations for
earthwork related items are presented in the following sections of this report Discussion
and recommendations for the design of structures such as the bridge foundation retaining
walls box culverts etc are presented in Section VI of this report
A Earthwork
Based on the plans provided and the rolling topography at the project site
earthwork for the proposed Package D roadway construction will involve excavations on

the order of about 26 meters deep and embankments up to about 20 meters thick
The majority of the embankment fill materials will be generated from the planned
excavations along the proposed alignments Based on the geologic conditions along the
proposed alignments we anticipate that the excavated materials would range from very
dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock to medium stiff to very stiff saprolite soils
In addition the earthwork construction will also encounter some soft and or loose recent
alluvial mangrove swamp and coralline lagoonal deposits

1 Cut Slope Design
Based on the subsurface conditions anticipated along the proposed alignments we
believe that the planned cut slopes may expose materials ranging from medium stiff
to very stiff saprolite materials to very dense and or hard volcanic breccia and tuff
rock formation In general we believe that a cut slope inclination of 1H 1V or flatter
may be used for the design of the planned cut slopes along the proposed
alignments In addition it is our opinion that a cut slope inclination as steep as
may be used along the North Route or in other localized areas where
very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock formation are encountered
Where the steeper cut slope inclination is used for cut slope design in rock
formation a rockfall catchment ditch should be provided at the toe of the steep rock
cut slope General guidelines for the design of the rockfall catchment ditch are
provided on Plate 4 of this report At this time we understand that the steeper rock
cut slope will be implemented at the Ngaraard Connecting Road We recommend
that Geolabs Hawaii be consulted for any other planned cut slope where a cut
slope inclination steeper than 1H 1V is desired
W O 3595 00 D Page 34
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
As previously indicated we anticipate that the proposed roadway alignments may
traverse areas with pre existing buried faults and joints which may result in
potential block type failure of the planned cut slopes Therefore it is our opinion
that planned cut slopes at these areas may need to be modified with a flatter slope
inclination that matches the angle of these potential slip planes These areas will
not be evident until exposed by the excavation process during construction
Therefore the cut slopes should be mapped by an engineer geologist from our
office or a qualified engineer geologist during construction to further evaluate the
cut slopes
Excessive surface run off over the slope face may cause erosion of the exposed
soils thus potentially jeopardizing the long term stability and performance of the cut
slope Therefore cut slopes should be protected by appropriate slope planting or
by other means such as placement of geotextile fabrics on the slope face
immediately after the slope is excavated to reduce the potential for erosion of the
exposed soils Detailed discussions pertaining to the use of geotextile fabrics on
the slope face are presented in the Erosion Control section of this report
For cut slopes with vertical heights greater than 15 meters we recommend that a
minimum 2 4 meter wide bench be provided at the mid point of the slope to reduce
the potential for erosion due to surface run off water The slope benches may be
omitted for cut slopes in the very dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formation encountered along the North Route and in other localized areas Where
slope benches are provided drainage ditches should be provided on the benches
to collect and divert surface water on the slopes to appropriate discharge outlets
The drainage ditches and discharge outlets should be lined with a minimum 50 mm
thick fiber reinforced shotcrete or gunite or 100 mm concrete to reduce erosion
from the concentrated flows
In addition interceptor drainage ditches should be considered at the top of the cut
slopes to provide proper drainage of surface run off water Interceptor drainage
ditches with steep grades may be susceptible to erosion and may require lining with
W O 3595 00 D Page 35
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
a minimum 50 mm thick fiber reinforced shotcrete or gunite In lieu of the shotcrete
or gunite lining consideration may be given to the use of 100 mm thick concrete or
other channel lining material such as turf reinforcement mats
Due to budgetary constraints we understand that the slope benches recommended
in our preliminary geotechnical engineering report and above will likely be
eliminated entirely for the Palau Compact Road project We believe that elimination
of slope benches along certain segments of the roadway alignments may result in
potential for instability of the planned cut slopes such as sloughing and or localized
slope failures Therefore the Owner should be made aware that this will probably
result in a more vigorous slope repair and roadway maintenance program in the
future
It should be noted that the planned cut slopes of 1H 1V slope ratio are steep
Therefore in the event that slight over cutting of a slope occurs or the cut slope is
slightly damaged by erosion consideration should be given to leaving the slope as
is rather than attempting to backfill the slope to the design grade with sliver fills
If backfilling of an over cut slope is necessary over steepened or unstable the cut
slope should be completely over cut and buttressed with compacted fill 8 meters
wide constructed of cement treated subbase by keying and benching the fill
materials into the over cut slope
2 Fill Slope Design
As previously mentioned the on site saprolite soils have high in situ moisture
contents Considering the high moisture contents of the on site soils the
compaction criteria have been reduced from the normal 90 percent to a minimum of
85 percent relative compaction in order to aid the earthwork construction in this
high rainfall environment using high moisture tropical soils In general permanent
embankment fills constructed with the lower compaction criteria over firm to stiff
ground should be designed with a slope inclination no steeper than 2H 1V to
account for the reduced fill strength
W O 3595 00 D eT Page 36
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
If the conditions warrant a steeper fill slope inclination fill slopes may be designed
with a slope inclination as steep as 1H 1V except in areas where soft subsoils are
anticipated provided that the fill slopes are reinforced with geogrids or similar
materials as discussed in the Reinforced Earth Slopes section of this report
We recommend that Geolabs Hawaii be consulted for site specific
recommendations for any planned fill slope with a slope inclination steeper than
2H 1V along the proposed roadway alignments

Excessive water should be diverted away from the tops of slopes and slope

for the planned fill slopes except at site specific locations Where slope benches
are necessary we recommend that a minimum 2 4 meter wide bench be provided
at the mid point of the slope to reduce the potential for erosion due to surface
run off water Construction of earth berms interceptor drainage ditches and the
use of geotextile fabrics over the fill slope face should be considered to reduce the
potential for erosion thus enhancing the long term stability of the planned fill

3 Subdrainage
Seepage conditions may be present at localized areas along the proposed roadway
alignments as evident in some areas noted during our site reconnaissance
Therefore we recommend that provisions be incorporated into the construction
documents to provide for subdrains in the following areas
at all springs and seepage areas
at the bottom of all canyon fills
on the uphill side of keyways and
in other areas of the site where seepage is observed during and after
grading or as recommended by the Engineer during construction
At stream crossings and other spring seepage areas where drainage features such
as reinforced box and pipe culverts are planned it is our opinion that a subdrain
system for subterranean seepage would not be necessary We believe that the
bedding material underneath the drainage structures may serve as a subdrain
system in these areas
Where needed subdrains should consist of perforated pipes with perforations
placed facing down and should be at least 100 mm in diameter All subdrains
should be surrounded and underlain by at least 100 mm of drain rock A non woven
geotextile such as Mirafi 180N or equivalent should wrap around the drain rock
In general subdrain trenches should be at least 300 mm wide and at least 600 mm
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
deep A sketch of the Typical Subdrain Details is presented on Plate 6 Subdrains
should be daylighted into drainage ditches culverts or other drainage structures for
proper discharge
4 Site Preparation
It should be noted that the existing terrain along the majority of the Palau Compact
Road alignments is heavily vegetated Therefore substantial site preparation work
involving clearing and grubbing would be required for the subject project At the
on set of earthwork areas within the contract grading limits should be thoroughly
cleared and grubbed In areas where mangrove plants are present the existing
ground should be cleared of the surface vegetation prior to the placement of
geogrids and a stabilization layer Grubbing of the mangrove areas would be very
difficult and will not be required All vegetation debris rubbish and other
unsuitable materials should be removed and disposed of properly beyond the limits
of grading to reduce the potential for contamination of the excavated materials
Soft and yielding areas encountered during clearing and grubbing below any areas
designated to receive fill not designated as soft soil areas should be
over excavated to expose firm natural material The resulting excavation should be
backfilled with well compacted general fill The excavated soft soils should be
properly disposed of beyond the limits of grading
Based on our field exploration results significant soft soil deposits may be
encountered along some portions of the roadway alignments We understand that
complete removal and replacement of soft soil deposits may not be feasible in
these areas due to the significant depth and areal extent of the soft soil deposits
encountered Therefore these areas should be stabilized in general accordance
with the recommendations presented in the Soft Ground Stabilization section of
this report prior to fill placement It should be noted that where soft ground
conditions are present a settlement waiting period and settlement monitoring would
be required
W O 3595 00 D SEELABS AWAD Page 40
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
In general the over excavated subgrades and areas designated to receive fills
should be proof rolled to a minimum of 85 percent relative compaction Relative
compaction refers to the in place dry density of soil expressed as a percentage of
the maximum dry density of the same soil established in accordance with
ASTM Test Designation D T 180 using the moist preparation
method wet to dry Optimum moisture is the water content corresponding to the
maximum dry density Saturation and subsequent yielding of the exposed
subgrade due to inclement weather and poor drainage may require over excavation
of the soft areas and replacement with compacted general fill
Our field exploration indicated that the in situ soils along the proposed roadway
alignments generally exist in a very moist to wet condition Therefore it would be
very difficult to achieve the normal 90 percent relative compaction requirement
without significant aeration of the in situ soils Since the project site is located in an
area that is subjected to high rainfall throughout the year substantial aeration of the
in situ soils may not be feasible and practical during the project construction As a
result we believe that the compaction requirement will need to be lowered to a
minimum of 85 percent relative compaction for subgrade preparation and fill
placement operations Use of the vibratory action of a compactor should be
carefully controlled to avoid inducing a pumping subgrade condition Detailed
discussions are presented in the Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements
subsection of this report
If the subgrade soils are pumping or yielding during subgrade preparation the
subgrade should be stabilized prior to fill placement and or pavement construction
Subgrade stabilization measures may include the use of additives such as cement
or lime treatment and or the incorporation of ground stabilization fabrics Detailed
discussions are presented in the Subgrade Stabilization section of this report
5 Fills and Backfills
In general we believe that the excavated materials may be used as a source of
general fill for embankment construction provided that the materials are properly
W O 3595 00 D SEOLABS HAWAII Page 41
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
processed and placed in accordance with the recommendations presented in the
Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements subsection of this report
Soft and or loose materials generated from excavations into the recent alluvial and
mangrove swamp deposits should not be used as fills and should be disposed of
properly beyond the limits of grading
Granular fills will be required for the construction of the causeway embankment and
in other designated areas Granular fill should be well graded from coarse to fine
with no particles larger than 150 mm in largest dimension and should contain not
more than 30 percent particles less than The material should have a
laboratory CBR value of 20 or more and should have a maximum swell value of
1 percent or less We believe that granular materials obtained from dredging in
parts of Palau may be used as a potential source of granular fill provided that the
material is free of clay lumps or balls processed to meet the project specifications
and compacted to the specified requirements
Surge rock fill should consist of clean gravel crushed stone rock or coral and
should be free from organic vegetable matter or other deleterious substances
The material should be free draining graded and range in size from 30 mm to
300 mm
Drain rock should consist of clean gravel crushed stone rock or coral and
should be free from organic vegetable matter or other deleterious substances
The material should be free draining and range in size from 10 mm to 40 mm
Fill and backfill materials within the upper 1 meter from the finished subgrades
should consist of materials less than 150 mm in largest dimension Materials
generated from excavations into the dense volcanic breccia and hard tuff rock
formations may be used as a source of fill and backfill materials within the upper
1 meter from the finished subgrades provided that they are screened of over sized
materials greater than 150 mm in largest dimension and processed to provide a
relatively well graded material to prevent the occurrence of voids in the compacted
W O 3595 00 D Page 42
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
mass Fill materials placed within future utility corridors should also be less than
150 mm in maximum dimension to facilitate future utility trench excavations
Over sized rock fragments may be disposed of off site used in deep fills or broken
down to smaller sized materials and incorporated into the fill materials If the
excavated rock materials do not contain sufficient smaller sized materials to
produce a well graded material off site borrow or on site rock crushing of
large sized rock fragments or boulders should be considered to provide the
required gradation and particle size to develop a well graded material In general
placement of boulders in fills should be in accordance with the procedures
recommended in the Boulder Disposal subsection of this report
6 Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements
Since the project site is located in a high rainfall area and the on site materials
generally have high in situ moisture contents ranging from about 50 to over
80 percent which is approximately 20 to 50 percent above the optimum moisture
content significant drying of the excavated materials will be required prior to their
use as fill and or backfill material in order to meet the normal 90 percent minimum
compaction requirement
As mentioned earlier substantial aeration of the in situ soils may not be feasible
due to the high rainfall environment at the project site Based on past project
experience in Palau and our experience with similar high moisture tropical soils we
believe that the compaction requirement for general fill placement for this project
may be reduced from the standard of 90 percent to a minimum of 85 percent
relative compaction Relative compaction refers to the in place dry density of soil
expressed as a percentage of the maximum dry density of the same soil
established in accordance with ASTM _ Test Designation D 1557 91
AASHTO T 180 using the moist preparation method wet to dry Optimum
moisture is the water content corresponding to the maximum dry density
The reduction in compaction criteria will result in a reduction in the shear strength of
the fill materials however we believe that sufficient strength can be obtained with
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
the lower compaction criteria for the proposed embankments However settlement
of the fills due to self weight especially in deep fills areas should be expected and
is further discussed in the Ground Settlement section of this report
Fills and backfills up to the finished subgrade of the pavement should be
moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture content placed in level lifts on
the order of about 150 to 200 mm in loose thickness and compacted to at least
85 percent relative compaction Even with the reduced 85 percent minimum
compaction criteria we believe that some moisture reduction would still be
necessary especially for materials generated from the deep excavations where the
in situ moisture contents may be in excess of 65 to 70 percent
The Contractor working on this project should be made aware that aeration to lower
the soil moisture and more compaction effort of thinner fill lifts to achieve the
specified compaction will generally reduce the rate of fill placement for this project
Compaction should be accomplished by sheepsfoot rollers vibratory rollers or
other types of acceptable compaction equipment Water tamping jetting or
ponding should not be allowed to compact the on site silty and clayey soils Due to
the high rainfall environment at the project site we believe that good construction
practices such as sealing and grading of the ground surface to provide positive
drainage at the end of each work day to reduce the potential for ponding and
saturation are essential to the earthwork operations for the proposed roadway
project
Where granular fills are used for earthwork construction such as for the causeway
fills and other areas we recommend that the compaction requirement for granular
fill materials be increased to a minimum of 90 percent relative compaction
In general granular fills should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum
moisture content placed in level loose lifts not exceeding about 200 mm and
compacted to not less than 90 percent relative compaction
W O 3595 00 D SOLAS HARI Page 44
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
Preparation and compaction of the pavement and shoulder subgrades and
placement and compaction of the subbase course aggregate base course cement
treated subbase and cement treated base are further discussed in the Subgrade
Subbase and Base Preparation section of this report

B Reinforced Earth Slopes
As discussed earlier under the Fill Slope Design subsection of this report a fill
slope inclination steeper than 2H 1V may be required in localized areas along the
proposed roadway alignments due to site specific conditions In general we believe that
fill slopes may be designed with slope inclinations as steep as 1H 1V provided that the
earth materials are reinforced with reinforced slope geogrids or geotextiles to strengthen
the fill soils
Reinforced slope geogrids are generally polymer grid structures with high tensile
strength It generally provides a cost effective solution to slope stability problems which
may include the following insufficient right of way high surcharge loads poor quality fills
high seismic forces steep slopes or difficult landslide repairs When reinforced slope
geogrids are placed in soil the grid geometry interlocks with adjacent soil creating a
soil geogrid composite with greatly enhanced engineering properties Different grid
configurations are available to provide optimum soil grid interaction for a range of soil
types and slope reinforcement applications Reinforced slope geotextile work in a similar
manner to reinforced slope georids The construction methodology is briefly described as
follows
W O 3595 00 D Page 48
GEOLABS HAWAII
SECTION V DISCUSSION AND EARTHWORK RECOMMENDATIONS
As the slope is constructed horizontal layers of reinforced slope geogrids or
geotextiles are placed in the compacted fill at predetermined levels The lengths of the
reinforced slope geogrid or geotextile layers are designed to anchor potential failure zones
into stable interior sections of the embankment or hillside As forces develop within a soil
mass the high modulus reinforced slope geogrids or geotextiles are immediately pulled
into tension The reinforced slope geogrids or geotextiles transfer this tensile force from
the unstable soil back into less stressed portions of the slope and stability is thus
maintained
Based on the preliminary grading plans we understand that reinforced earth fill
slopes with a slope inclination of 1H 1V is planned on the left side of the roadway
alignment from about to of the North Route As discussed under
the Fill Slope Design subsection of this report we understand that fill slopes with a
slope inclination of are planned along some portions of the Package D
alignments It is our opinion that reinforced slope geogrids or geotextiles should be
incorporated into the design of these fill slopes where the fill height is over 4 meters as
shown in the following table

material general fill we believe that a friction angle on the order of 28 to 30 degrees and
a wet density of about m may be used for the preliminary design analyses of the

may be used for the foundation soils We recommend that a minimum of 2 meters of
